Speech by Wang Yongbin, Minister of Judicial Administration 125

Wang Yongbin, Minister of Judicial Administration, arrived in Shanghai from Nanjing at around 6:00 am on the 9th of this month. He first inspected the Second Prison directly under the Ministry and broadcast a speech to the prisoners. Then he went to the Zhenru Forensic Medical Research Institute to preside over the graduation ceremony of the researchers and examiners of the Institute and delivered a speech. All the chief officials of the Shanghai courts attended, and the ceremony was very grand. After the ceremony, he returned to Nanjing in the afternoon of the same day. The main points of Minister Wang's speech are recorded as follows:

(1) Speech at the Zhenru Forensic Medical Research Institute: The general idea is that today is the graduation ceremony of the researchers and examiners of the Forensic Medical Research Institute. I, as the Minister, deeply believe that the training of forensic medical researchers is still a pioneering undertaking in the judicial circles of our country, and the responsibilities that you will bear in the future are extremely important. Now that you are graduating, I have come to Shanghai from Nanjing to preside over the ceremony. Criminal trials are valued in discovering the truth. In the past era of torture and confession, all criminal facts were based on the confessions of criminals, and the facts of forced confessions were everywhere. The so-called "under the three woods, what cannot be obtained?" The construction of unjust cases was by no means accidental. Since the reform, the system of torture has been absolutely rejected, and the discovery of criminal facts depends entirely on evidence. Therefore, Article 270, Paragraph 2 of the Criminal Procedure Law states that even if the defendant has confessed, other necessary evidence should still be investigated to see if it is consistent with the facts. It is very clear that the position of confession in today's trial is almost irrelevant. However, the nature of evidence depends on the evolution of social conditions, the progress of science, and the ever-changing methods of crime. Whether most of the evidence is reliable cannot be identified by experts. Although the power of collecting evidence rests with the judge, the identification of the authenticity of most evidence and the examination of deaths and injuries are the responsibility of you. Therefore, the responsibilities that you will bear in the future cannot be said to be not important. I, as the Minister, have deep and urgent expectations for you. Since the implementation of the Court Organization Law, the number of courts at all levels has increased sharply, and the need for forensic doctors is increasingly felt. However, limited by funds and time, it has not been possible to train a large number of talents in a short period of time to meet the needs of the courts in various provinces. However, I, as the Minister, am planning to enrich the Forensic Medical Research Institute and continue to train a large number of forensic medical personnel. Since you are pioneers, I firmly believe that you will be able to base your knowledge and fulfill your duties to be the model for those who come later.

(2) Broadcasting Speech at the Second Prison directly under the Ministry of Justice: The general idea is that I, as the Minister, have come to Shanghai due to official business, and in the midst of my busy schedule, I have come to inspect this prison. I have seen that the residences, food, and clothing of the prisoners are all clean and hygienic, and the prisoners are working diligently, which is very satisfactory. However, the country has spent hundreds of thousands of dollars to build this huge prison. Its purpose is not for the comfort of you prisoners, but to emphasize education as the purpose of modern punishment. You have violated the national criminal punishment regulations and have been sentenced by the court and transferred here to be executed. It is like sending a sick person to a hospital for treatment. In the future, when you are released from prison or have credible repentance, you will be granted parole according to the law, just like a patient who has recovered from illness and left the hospital. Therefore, you should, during the execution of your sentence, inspire your conscience, wash away your past mistakes, abide by prison rules, and accept teachings, so that you can become good citizens in the future, and how you should especially strive to work diligently to acquire a skill to make a living after being released from prison. You must know that the more evil people there are in the country, the more the country loses its vitality. The more good people there are in the country, the more the country increases its vitality. Although there are various reasons for your crimes in the past, the lack of a correct outlook on life is one of them. This prison is directly under the Ministry, and all teaching and work are more complete. I, as the Minister, deeply hope that after you leave this prison in the future, you will surely become good citizens and increase the country's vitality. This is what I expect.

Eyes Blinded by Lime, 1,800 Gold Stolen 128

At around 10:40 yesterday morning, at the intersection of Fujian Road and Ningbo Road, a middle-aged man was passing by when two robbers who had been lying in ambush suddenly jumped out to rob him. One robber held a bag of lime, and the other held a gun. The robber with the bag threw the lime bag at the man's face, causing him to be unable to open his eyes. The robbers took the opportunity to search the man's body, stealing more than 1,800 yuan that he had hidden and fleeing without a trace. The man was blinded and unable to follow. He frantically shouted for help. By the time the nearby policemen heard the alarm and arrived, it was too late. They immediately reported to the police station and sent a car to rush him to the hospital for treatment. They also sent detectives to pursue the robbers. 2,000 Dollars in Cash Stolen, Robber Gang Has Handguns

The Case of Japanese Sailor Nakayama Hideo: Zhou Sherong Released; Yang Wendao's Appeal Filed with the Court Yesterday Morning 131

Yang Wendao, Ye Haisheng, and Zhou Sherong, all from Guangdong, were prosecuted by the Public Concession Police for the shooting death of Japanese sailor Nakayama Hideo on Doule'an Road on November 9th of last year. The Special Court No. 1 has already tried the case, sentencing Yang and Ye to death and acquitting Zhou. Following the verdict, Yang and Ye separately filed appeals with the High Court's Second Branch. As for Zhou Sherong, the police have confirmed that they will not appeal further. Yesterday morning, the police lawyer, Ru Baoyi, declared to Qian Hongye, the head of the Criminal Division of Special Court No. 1, that they were abandoning the appeal against Zhou and requested his immediate release. Judge Qian ordered Zhou Sherong's release. Ye Haisheng's appeal has already been recorded in this newspaper. Yang Wendao's wife, Mrs. Tang, commissioned lawyer Tang Huaiqun to draft an appeal on behalf of her husband, Yang Wendao, which was also submitted to the High Court's Second Branch yesterday morning, requesting that the original judgment be overturned and Yang Wendao be declared innocent. The original statement is as follows:

Appellant: Yang Wendao, Case No. 893 of the 24th Year of the Republic, the Public Works Bureau's Disraeli Road Police Station versus Yang Wendao for conspiring to murder Japanese sailor Nakayama Hideo. Dissatisfied with the first instance judgment, he hereby submits an appeal and supplementary reasons. Upon review of the first instance judgment by the First Special District Court, Yang Wendao was convicted of murdering Japanese sailor Nakayama Hideo and sentenced to death. An appeal has been duly filed within the prescribed time limit. After studying the contents of the judgment, the grounds on which Yang Wendao's guilt and sentence were based are twofold: (1) a physics book with a gun-shaped hole, and (2) Ye Haisheng's confession. However, whether these two points can serve as the basis for a conviction, considering the circumstances of the previous court hearings and corroborating evidence, constitutes a grave injustice that requires separate explanation and presentation.

Regarding the Book with a Gun-Shaped Hole

After Yang Wendao was arrested, although he admitted in court on April 20th that the physics book with a gun-shaped hole presented by the police belonged to him, he stated on April 27th that the book was not his and that he had previously owned another one. The former was a frank admission without any hesitation, while the latter was a sudden change of heart. Those who do not pay attention to the facts might suspect him of being cunning and firmly believe that the book is ironclad evidence of guilt. However, after examining both past and present circumstances, the truth will become clear without detailed explanation. (Yang Wendao borrowed a pistol from his friend Li Mu in the 22nd year of the Republic and registered it with the Public Works Bureau for self-defense. However, fearing that his many children might play with it and cause an accident, he asked his cousin Yang Jianzhong for a method of hiding it by cutting a hole in a book. He immediately used an English physics book to create a hiding place. Later, the gun was returned, and the book became useless and was discarded, left for his children to play with. The day after his arrest, the police found the book in his house and took it back to the police station. Although they did not ask, Yang Wendao immediately said that the book belonged to him (according to Deputy Inspector Crowe's report)). It is clear that Yang Wendao did not consider this book to be of any importance, and his confession in court on April 20th shows his frankness. If the book were indeed part of a criminal act, there would be no reason to keep it at home for a long time, nor would he be foolish enough to directly admit ownership. Therefore, the origin of the book must be investigated. Thus, Yang Wendao's admission to the book, and his later claim that it was planted by his cousin Yang Jianzhong, warrant further investigation. It is alleged that Yang Jianzhong is of bad character, fierce by nature, and known to his fellow villagers and friends. If a secret investigation is conducted, it will not be difficult to find out that several days before Yang Wendao's arrest, his clan member Yang Guimei told him that he was suspected of something and should flee quickly. When Yang Wendao asked about the source of this information, he said it was relayed by Yang Jianzhong. When Yang Wendao eagerly wanted to bring him to meet Yang Jianzhong, he hesitated and could not answer, and was often slapped in the face by Yang Wendao in anger. This happened before, so Yang Jianzhong is likely to have premeditated this case. In addition, the testimony of witness Zhang Chen and the interconnectedness of witnesses Hui Yuan and Zheng Pingshan presented by the police (as detailed in the appeal by lawyer Zhang Zhizhang on behalf of Ye Haisheng) suggest that Yang Jianzhong's framing is not without cause. However, the fingerprints and palm prints taken from Yang Jianzhong and submitted to the Forensic Institute for examination, after detailed comparison, did not reveal any similar patterns to the fingerprints left in the book. Therefore, the claim that Yang Jianzhong framed him is considered unsupportable. Generally, if someone is planting evidence, does the evidence necessarily have to have their fingerprints and palm prints to prove it? We will set that aside for now. However, since the book had been kept in Yang Wendao's house for a long time, why is it that the fingerprints and palm prints of Yang Wendao, examined repeatedly by the Forensic Institute at the request of the original court and compared with the fingerprints found in the book, did not reveal any similarities, and the bloody fingerprints in the book did not match Yang Wendao's fingerprints and palm prints? (All seen in the Institute's various examination reports). Is there any reason for this? The original court ignored this important issue. Not only is the determination of facts clearly wrong, but the judgment that the book does not have Yang Jianzhong's fingerprints is also unfair. Furthermore, according to the internal reports of the Forensic Institute, if the dirt and pressure marks on each page are as deep as they appear, why are the cut marks in the hole, which must have been used for a long time, still so neat and new? This is impossible, as everyone knows. The original court did not pay attention to this, which is puzzling. If this book with the gun-shaped hole presented in evidence is immediately used as evidence to convict Yang Wendao, it is unreasonable and inconceivable.

Regarding Ye Haisheng's Confession

Ye Haisheng's confession, as seen in the court transcripts, is contradictory and insincere (as detailed in the appeal by lawyer Zhang Zhizhang). Therefore, the sections involving Yang Wendao are not credible. Furthermore, Yang Wendao has never admitted the facts of the conspiracy to murder as stated by Ye Haisheng. Ye also stated that a Korean, Jack, participated in the conspiracy. However, when questioned in court, Jack and Yang Wendao did not know each other. If it were indeed a premeditated joint murder, this important matter could not be entrusted to someone unknown. Therefore, given the complexity and darkness of the case's inside story, how can Ye Haisheng's confession, involving Yang Wendao, be considered the basis for a conviction? It goes without saying that this is a miscarriage of justice. The original court completely ignored evidence favorable to the defendant, which is truly regrettable. In light of the above facts and reasons, it is clear that the occurrence of this case is entirely due to a conspiracy by false witnesses Zheng Pingshan, Zeng Yuan, Zhang Zhi, Yang Jianzhong, and others to frame him. The death of Japanese sailor Nakayama Hideo has nothing to do with the defendant Yang Wendao. Apart from the reasons for defense in this case, which have already been detailed in the appeal by lawyer Zhang Zhizhang on behalf of the second defendant, Ye Haisheng, and will not be repeated, we hereby submit to your honor, hoping that you will be gracious and grant a secret investigation, revoke the original judgment, and declare Yang Wendao innocent and release him, thereby redressing the miscarriage of justice, bringing the dead back to life and returning flesh to bones, which would be a true act of kindness. Respectfully submitted, [to] the Jiangsu High Court Second Branch. [Submitted by] Yang Wendao's wife, Yang Tangshi; [Drafted by] Lawyer Tang Huaiqun.

Car Accident Injures Five People 133

Wu Liu Dies; Police Sue Driver

On the 9th of this month, at 4:15 PM, in front of the British-owned Public Omnibus Company on Connaught Road, a car with license plate number 8284, driven by Cai Guomin, was towing a newly repaired car with Chinese license plate number 5651 (driven by Chen Guixing, a coppersmith from the Gordon Road Repair Shop) in an easterly direction. At that time, a handcart pushed by Gong A'er from Chongming, with a carpenter named Gu Maomao sitting on it, and a piece of lumber eighteen feet long, along with other planks, was also moving forward in the same direction. Cai wanted to pass the handcart, so he turned the wheel to the right. However, Chen, who was not skilled in driving, did not turn the wheel, causing him to crash into the lumber. As a result, the cart and people fell to the ground, and a woman from Yancheng, Wu Liu, and her two children were also injured. In total, there were five injured men, women, and children. However, because Wu Liu's injuries were the most severe, she was sent to Guangren Hospital, but treatment was ineffective, and she died at 4:30 AM on the 10th. The body was taken to the forensic examination center on Faelun Road. The others were sent to the hospital. After being bandaged, they had already left the hospital for treatment. The Gordon Road Police Station, after investigation, determined that Chen Guixing was suspected of negligent homicide and arrested him. Yesterday morning, he was handed over to the First Special Court for prosecution. Because further investigation was needed, the police requested an extension. Later, Zhang Qiru, a prosecutor from the court's Procuratorate, arrived at the forensic examination center. The examination revealed that the deceased, Wu Liu, female, was struck by a car and lumber, resulting in her death. The body was handed over to her husband, Wu Changzhu, for burial. Chen Guixing, the perpetrator, has been prosecuted by the police and handed over to the court for legal proceedings.

Robbery on Caoxi Road; Victim Stabbed 134

Pan Bosheng, a local resident, 31 years old, who lives downstairs at the south end of Caohejing Town, Shanghai West, and grows flowers, took a rickshaw yesterday at around 2 AM, carrying fresh flowers to Shanghai for sale. When he arrived at the south end of Caoxi Road and Zhongshan Road, near the Shanghai-Hangzhou Railway, a bandit suddenly jumped out of the darkness and blocked Pan's path. Pan Bosheng, knowing they were up to no good, shouted for help. The bandit pulled out a sharp blade and stabbed Pan's right leg and right arm four times, causing him to fall to the ground. A patrolman heard the sound and rushed over, but the bandit had already fled far away. Pan Bosheng was escorted home and was treated at the Red Cross Hospital on Haige Road yesterday.

Discrepancy Between Pledged Goods and Description; Seventy-Year-Old Man Accused; Description States Over 1200 Dozen Undershirts; Inspection Reveals Only Over 300 Dozen 135

Zhang Wanyi, a man from Sichuan, 70 years old, established the Zhang Wanyi firm at No. 1 Taideli, West Zigaihuo Street. On January 31st of last year, Zhang used a warehouse receipt from the Donglai Bank to pledge goods at the Zhicheng Money Shop at No. x, Jiyang Lane, Henan Road. The receipt stated that there were forty boxes of goods, but did not specify the detailed contents of the boxes. Zhang further wrote a receipt stating that the boxes contained 1255 dozen men's and women's undershirts, worth a total of 18,212 yuan. After negotiation, a pledge of 12,000 yuan was made for a term of three months. After the pledge agreement was made, Zhang first paid back 2,000 yuan to the Zhicheng Money Shop on April 1st, and then paid interest of 120 yuan in May. After that, there was no news. Although Zhicheng Money Shop repeatedly urged him to redeem the goods, Zhang tried to delay. Recently, because Zhang had no intention of redeeming the goods, Zhicheng Money Shop exercised its right of mortgage and inspected the boxes at the Donglai Bank warehouse at No. 881 Suzhou Road. It was found that the forty boxes contained only 380 dozen undershirts, which was more than two-thirds less than the number Zhang stated on the receipt. However, the warehouse facilities were in good condition, and there was no possibility of theft. It was clear that Zhang had committed fraud. The manager of the shop, Qin Zhenfu, hired lawyers Jiang Baoli and Jiang Pingfan to report the matter to the General Police Station. Chinese detective Yang Peisheng and detective Kang Zengxiang went to No. 1 Hede Road and arrested Zhang, and entrusted the second landlord of the house, Hu Yunfei, to take care of the items Zhang left behind. Zhang was taken back to the police station and detained. Yesterday morning, he was handed over to the Second Criminal Division of the Special Court. Police lawyer Qian Xunjiu stated the facts and prosecuted him for fraud under Article 349 of the Criminal Law. He stated that Zhang Wanyi had confessed to the crime at the police station. However, he claimed that the matter was not his master plan, but was instigated by Sheng Mengli (residing at No. 17 Gaofu Lane, Pushi Road, French Concession), the deputy manager of Zhicheng Money Shop, and the second landlord, Hu Yunfei. Therefore, the police are currently investigating and requested that the court postpone the case. After Judge Pan Zhenyang interrogated Zhang, he ordered the defendant to be remanded in custody and rescheduled the hearing.

Winners to be Announced Next Month

Award Method

This exhibition has too few things that resist."

The Tongyi Bank Shareholders' Meeting Resolved to Dissolve Immediately 141

Xu Yongzuo Appointed as Liquidator

After the Tongyi Bank suspended operations in January of last year, it entrusted accountant Xu Yongzuo to investigate the accounts, collect debts, and settle debts. Shareholders' meetings were convened twice last year to discuss plans for progress, but both times the number of shareholders present was insufficient to meet the legal requirements, and no decision could be made. Yesterday afternoon at 2 PM, another extraordinary shareholders' meeting was held at the Xu Accountant Firm on Avenue Edward VII. The number of attendees met the legal requirements. Yu Huanzheng was elected as chairman. The chairman first asked accountant Xu to report on the progress. He briefly stated that the bank's external debt at the time of the suspension of operations was as high as 3.2 to 3.3 million yuan. It has been gradually settled since then, and only about 700,000 yuan remains outstanding. The chairman asked the attendees to discuss plans for progress. It was generally agreed that the current situation and market conditions are worse than at the time of the suspension, and there is no certainty of resumption of operations. With only 700,000 yuan of external debt remaining, it would be better to dissolve and liquidate immediately to bring the matter to an end. This was unanimously approved on the spot, and accountant Xu Yongzuo was elected as liquidator with full authority to handle liquidation matters.

Tragic Murder with Barber Scissors of an Adulterous Man; Zhang Meiyun Collaborates with His Wife's Younger Brother; Turns Vicious Against His Wife's Lover 143

Zhang Meiyun, also known as Xiao Shuangzi, a barber from Yangzhou, in his twenties, lived at No. 4 Yuedeli, Dongchang Road, Pudong. His wife, Feng Lanying, 23 years old, worked at the Lunchang Dyeing and Weaving Factory in Lujiazui. Despite her ordinary appearance, she was coveted and seduced by Zhang Liuchen (24 years old) from Shandong, who rowed boats at the Xiaonanyang Wharf near the factory, resulting in an affair. In May of this year, because of a lack of secrecy, the husband discovered the affair, arrested the adulterous couple, and handed them over to the Pudong Branch Bureau, which transferred them to the local court. As a result, the two sides reached a settlement. Unexpectedly, Zhang Liuchen and Feng Lanying still maintained contact, secretly meeting from time to time. Feng's younger brother, Baoguo, also a barber, felt that his sister's behavior was a disgrace to his family, so he conspired with his brother-in-law, Meiyun. At about 9 PM the night before last, they took a pair of barber scissors, disassembled them into two halves, each holding one half, went to Lujiazui, and called out Liuchen, pretending to go to Jiang Wencai's house at No. 2 Yangzhou Lane, Dongchang Road, to discuss the matter. When they reached Jiang's door, Feng Sanyi suddenly raised half a pair of scissors and stabbed Liuchen three times. He was stabbed once in the left waist, once in the inner side of the left thigh, and once in the inner side of the right thigh. The abdominal wound was the most severe, with organs flowing out. He fell to the ground, unconscious. Seeing that their goal had been achieved, the murderers, led by Meiyun, went to the Lunchang Factory to call out Lanying, and the three fled in different directions without a trace. The injured man was rushed to Pudong Hospital by witnesses Jiang Wencai and Zhao A'er, but he died before arriving. The body was taken to the hospital morgue to await examination. After the incident, Wang Shifu, the captain of the Pudong Detective Branch, ordered team leaders Chen Jinshan and Cheng Peizhang, and detectives Chang Zhao Bingquan, Li Shuren, and Cui Youkuan, to arrest the murderers separately. Yesterday morning at 2 AM, a suspicious woman named Guo Zhaodi was found at the Dongchang Road ferry. She stated that she lived in the city at Guangqi Road, Sipailou, and had known Feng Lanying before. She said, "Lanying came to my house to live, and ordered me to go to her house in Pudong to get clothes. I didn't expect to be arrested." The detectives got this lead and rushed to Pudong to arrest Lanying, who confessed that her husband was waiting in front of the Qingquan Bathhouse on Avenue Edward VII. The detectives rushed to the Qingquan Bathhouse, waiting until dawn, but there was no sign of him. As the clock struck five, they returned to the Dongmen Road Pier at the Sixteenth Bund and suddenly encountered the murderer Feng Baoguo guarding the ferry. Seeing the detectives and his sister arrive, he knew he had been exposed and tried to flee, but was caught by the detectives. Along with the team, after Zhang Jinlin, the coroner of the Pudong Branch Bureau, and witnesses Jiang Wencai and Zhao A'er interrogated the suspects, they were ordered to be sent to the General Bureau for questioning in the evening. At the same time, the search for the fugitive Zhang Meiyun was continued for further investigation. As for the body of the deceased, the bureau ordered the local guarantor Lu Shunlong to report to the local court. At 4 PM, prosecutor Kong was appointed to go to Pudong to examine the body. The examination revealed that the deceased had been stabbed in a vital area and died. The body was ordered to be prepared for burial by the family, pending further investigation.

Qianjiatang: Bloodshed Occurred Last Night; The Deceased Was Yin Bengen, Formerly a Detective 146

Last night (the 11th) at 11:00 PM, two men, one wearing a long black robe and the other wearing a white-grey shirt and trousers, were seen in the French Concession's Qianjiatang chasing a man in black shirt and trousers from west to east. The chase ended at the entrance of No. 168 Wujia Lane, in front of the house of a local woman named Shao Wang. The fleeing man, seeing that the gate of Shao Wang's house was not closed, was about to squat down and escape inside when the man in black clothes caught up and grabbed him. The man in white-grey shirt and trousers immediately drew a gun and fired several shots. The man in black shirt and trousers was hit by three bullets in the right side of his head, the back of his head, and under his ear. Blood gushed out like a tide. Seeing his objective achieved, the assailant turned and fled. Shao Wang, who was about to close her door to go to sleep, was shocked and dared not speak. After the assailant had gone far and she regained her composure, she reported the incident to the French police. It is reported that the deceased had previously served as a detective and had solved several theft cases. It is suspected that his murder is related to a grudge held by criminals from previous theft cases he solved.

The County Magistrate Doused with Caustic Soda Case: Important Evidence Discovered; Fang Aliu Testifies Vividly; Four Letters Provide Reference for the Case 148

Xu Xueseng, a native of Songjiang, over forty years old, formerly served as the County Magistrate of Zhangye in Gansu. He has resided in Shanghai for many years. On the evening of March 6 of this year, near Wangzhi Road in the French Concession, he was injured in the face by an assailant using corrosive liquid. The assailant, Gao Jinsheng, was riding a bicycle and attempted to flee in a panic during the attack. However, the bicycle suddenly fell, causing Gao to fall off the bicycle and also be splashed by the caustic soda, resulting in his immediate arrest. After trial by the Second Special District Court, he was sentenced to four years of imprisonment. Gao appealed, but his appeal was rejected. He is currently within the period for final appeal. Details have been reported in this newspaper previously. Since the incident, the victim, Xu Xueseng, has undergone a long period of treatment and has been fortunate to recover, but a large portion of his face has been destroyed, and his right eye is completely blind. It was later discovered that Zhu Guanghan, a fellow townsman currently residing at No. 4 Fuyangfang, Tongfu Road, in the Public Concession, and Chen Axi, the son of Zhu's old servant Chen Meilang, were suspected of instigating the assault. A lawyer was retained to file a complaint against Zhu and Chen at the Shanghai Local Court. Efforts were made to apprehend Chen Axi in the countryside of Wuxian County. He was arrested, brought to court, and interrogated. After several hearings, another hearing was held yesterday at 2:00 PM. Judge Yu Lude presided over the third criminal court. The lawyers for the plaintiff, Xu Xueseng, were Xu Lin and Wen Chao. The lawyers for the defendant, Zhu Guanghan, were Gu Changyuan, He Xianzhang, and Ding Zheming. First, the witness Jiang Weicheng was called to testify. Jiang stated that he was 49 years old, a native of Wuxian County, Jiangsu, residing at No. 486 Qipu Road. He was formerly a detective with the Public Concession Police Station and resigned two years ago. He currently runs a rice shop. He has no family relationship with either Xu or Zhu. Around the end of the lunar year last year, a friend surnamed Feng, whom he knew, came to his (Jiang's) house, saying that the sister of a woman named Fan Qian, who was married as a concubine to Zhu Guanghan, a merchant from Songjiang, was in a state of life and death unknown. Feng wanted to find and introduce a lawyer Zheng Wen to represent her in suing Zhu Guanghan and seeking 7,000 yuan in compensation through an incidental private suit. Feng knew that lawyer Zheng Wen's firm shared the same residence with him and that Zheng and he were good friends. He introduced Feng and Fan Qian to lawyer Zheng. After three negotiations, a settlement was reached, with Qian being compensated 1,000 yuan. One evening around 8:00 PM, Xu Xueseng suddenly arrived, saying that Zhu Guanghan had instructed him to come and that the settlement draft should be based on Zhu's own draft, not lawyer Zheng's. No one objected, and the settlement was completed. Zheng Wen and he acted as witnesses. This was the initial course of events. However, one morning in February of this year, Feng suddenly called him, asking if he knew that Xu Xueseng had been doused with caustic soda and told him to read the newspaper immediately. He bought a copy of the "Shishi Xinbao" and found out what had happened. Feng also arrived at the same time, claiming that if this matter were to escalate, they would trace it back to the settlement at the end of last year and that they might both be suspected. It would be best for them to step forward and fundamentally resolve the matter. However, lawyer Zheng's response was that Xu's injuries were too severe at this time and that they could not proceed until Xu's injuries had healed. When Xu's injuries showed slight improvement, they resumed negotiations. At that time, Xu demanded that Zhu Guanghan provide him with a living allowance of 500 yuan per month for fifteen years, totaling over 90,000 yuan. Feng claimed that Zhu did not have such financial resources. After repeated negotiations, Zhu was willing to pay Xu 10,000 yuan to settle the matter, and Xu agreed. Feng said that Zhu had returned to Songjiang to raise the money and would return to Shanghai by Tuesday or Wednesday. Unexpectedly, after waiting for three days, Feng called him again, saying that Zhu had only raised 2,000 yuan and that he intended to pay the rest with checks. This was too far off the mark, and there were various inconveniences with checks. He was really unable to get involved and could only declare his withdrawal. At this time, Zhu Guanghan was right next to the phone, waiting for a reply, but he absolutely refused to participate. At this point, Feng withdrew from all involvement. However, several days later, a man named Zhu Mengwei, a member of Xu Xueseng's clan, also intended to mediate, but it was ultimately unsuccessful. This was the true account of what he had experienced. At this point, lawyer Xu Lin stood up and stated that during the court recess, the plaintiff, Xu Xueseng, had obtained from Fang Aliu, a friend of Gao Jinsheng, the assailant who was in custody, four letters and notes sent by Gao Jinsheng from prison. The letters detailed how he instructed Chen Axi's father, Chen Meilang, to contact Zhu Guanghan quickly, how lawyer Gu Changyuan went to see him, how lawyer Gu promised him a reward, and how he instructed his aunt to go to the firm to collect money. He requested that the judge examine them in detail. He then presented the letters to the court. Finally, lawyer Xu stated that the witness Fang Aliu was now in court and requested that he be examined. Judge Yu ordered Fang to be brought before the court. Fang stated that he was 27 years old, a native of Cixi, Zhejiang, residing on Ximen Road in the French Concession. He had previously been in the beef business and was now unemployed. He further stated that Gao Jinsheng was a close friend of his. He had been sentenced to imprisonment by the First Special District Court for smoking opium and was released on January 23 of this year. After his release, he learned that Gao Jinsheng had been blinded by greed and used by others to attack someone with caustic soda and had been arrested and sentenced to four years. He had visited him once, but Gao still maintained his mindset of taking other people's money to solve other people's problems and refused to reveal the instigators. During a certain hearing, he (Fang) witnessed Xu Xueseng's tragic injuries at the courthouse door and felt compassion. He then arranged to meet Xu through someone and handed over the letters that lawyer Xu Lin had just presented to the court for use as evidence. If he was called to testify in court, he would certainly appear in court to confront them. This was his testimony. If he was found to have lied in any way, he would accept severe punishment. At this point, the official announced that the hearing would be adjourned, and that both parties must submit all evidence without delay. Finally, lawyer Xu Lin stated that Gao Jinsheng was an extremely poor vagrant before his imprisonment, but after his imprisonment, he suddenly became a temporary millionaire. The court was urged to investigate the Gao Jinsheng detention center to determine the amount of money currently in Gao's possession, which would provide an easy indication of the truth. The official stated that this was within the court's scope of authority and ordered Zhu Guanghan to remain released on bail and await further hearings. The hearing was adjourned, and it was already six o'clock, and the city was lit up when they left the courthouse.

The Hai Rui Steamer Encountered a Storm: Two Crew Members Drowned 149

The Cargo Was Damaged by Water

The Hai Rui steamer, owned by the state-run China Merchants Steam Navigation Company, with a deadweight of 2,049 tons, originally operated between Shanghai and Lianyungang. Recently, due to the accumulation of cargo on the South China route, the steamer was reassigned to the Shantou and Guangzhou route. This time, it loaded a large amount of cargo in Shanghai and first went to Shantou to unload. However, the ship encountered a severe storm off the port of Shantou. The waves were enormous. In the most dangerous moments, the waves crashed over the ship and directly into the pilothouse. Five bales of cotton on the deck were swept into the sea. Seawater also entered the large cargo hold, damaging part of the cargo. The losses were significant. Upon arriving in Shantou, it was necessary to first unload the cargo and handle the general average. The shipowner had already telegraphed the bureau to report the incident. However, when the ship arrived in Shantou, seven crew members boarded a sampan to go ashore. Before reaching the pier, a barge from the pier came from the outside and collided with the sampan. The sampan was already old and dilapidated. After the collision, it immediately leaked and sank into the harbor. The seven crew members also fell into the water. Five people were rescued on the spot, but two were still missing: one was the chief steward (the cook) of the Hai Rui, and the other was Tai Li (the cargo supervisor). Repeated searches failed to find even their bodies. The incident has been telegraphed to Shanghai. The Hai Rui will return to Shanghai after loading all the cargo at the ports in Guangzhou and Guangdong. A telegram was received yesterday stating that the ship was already on its return voyage. Detailed information about the incident will be available after the shipowner and purser arrive in Shanghai.

A Young Woman Committed Suicide for Love by Taking Poison 150

Her Lover Also Swallowed Opium Paste; As a Result, the Woman Died Tragically

Wang Zengjun, also known as Monk, a local man, 26 years old, worked as an ironing clerk at the Lao Shanghai Laundry Shop at No. 79 Hengmao Lane, Mintiniyin Road, in the French Concession. Jinshu regretted the marriage and could not bear to separate from Wang, so she decided to end her life. After taking the poison, Wang saw that Jinshu was still conscious and could be saved, so he took her and a companion to Puqing Hospital at No. 730 Guangdong Road for help. The hospital reported the incident to the police, who sent the body to the Tongren Fuyuan Branch Hall autopsy room. Wang was taken into custody for interrogation. Yesterday, Judge Wang, an inspector of the Second Special Court, arrived at the hall and confirmed that Shen Jinshu had died from poisoning. After questioning the deceased's mother, Shen Qian, and Wang Zengjun, the official ordered that the woman's body be handed over to her mother for burial.

They claim that he protected the defendants Li Guang and Liu Yulai and illegally detained them. Therefore, in addition to suing Ju, they are also suing Li Guang and Liu Yulai for assault and fraud. Yesterday, Judge Zhang Peiming held a joint hearing. Liu Yueming stated that he was 46 years old, from Yancheng, and resided at Zhangjiabang, north of Gaolangqiao. On September 29, he sold two pigs that he had raised. Li Guang and Liu Yulai demanded two dollars from him. Because he had no cash, they refused to allow him to sell the pigs. His friend Lu Shanben came out to mediate and was injured in one eye by them. When they went to the Fifth District Fourth Branch, the police chief instead detained them for three days and released them, ordering him to pay ten dollars as soon as he returned home, or else they would arrest him again. Therefore, he was suing them. Lu Shanben stated that he was 46 years old, from Funing. Li Guang, etc., demanded two dollars from Liu Yueming, who was selling pigs. Because he had no cash, they wanted to beat him. He went to persuade them and was also beaten by them. Li Guang stated that he was 35 years old, from Funing, and an employee of Chen Dexing Pig Shop. Because they were selling pigs privately, his boss told him and Liu Yulai to investigate. He told them to go to the pig shop together, but they beat him. They went to the police station to report the incident because they violated health regulations, so they were fined. Liu Yulai stated that he was 54 years old, from Funing, and his statement was the same as Li's. Police Chief Ju Jin stated that he was 40 years old, from Jiangyin, and the chief of the Yinxianggang Police Station. At the time of the incident, Li Guang reported to the Zhangjiahong Branch that the case was due to a fight and they were sent to the station. There was no mention of injuries, so they were each fined one dollar. Because Lu had no money, he was detained for one day. Liu Yueming was brought in by the police sergeant because he violated the health bureau's regulations and was fined two dollars and detained for two days. The official announced that the case should be investigated further and that another hearing would be held.

Son of Military Officer Kidnapped by Subordinates: Zhang Ziyun Confesses After One Interrogation; Accomplice Bao Chongfu Arrested 155

Yang Zhengqing, the former military commander of a certain army, has lived as a recluse in the main street of Minhang Town with his family since his retirement for several years. In July of this year, Yang's ten-year-old son, Abao, suddenly disappeared one day. Wang Yaotang, the police station's lawyer, agreed to the transfer. Bao Chongfu stated that he had a long-standing feud with Zhang Ziyun and that he had cheated him out of money. He was about to arrest him, but he falsely accused him first, which was hateful. Judge Fu ordered that Bao Chongfu be handed over to the officers from the Municipal Public Security Bureau to be taken back for interrogation and ordered that a formal official document be submitted for record.

Ye Ruizhen Sues Ye Zhongfang: Division of Deceased Father's Estate; Ruizhen is Illegitimate, Zhongfang Does Not Acknowledge; Court Orders Identity to be Confirmed First 156

Ye Huanyu, a Chinese comprador of the insurance department of the China Business Company on Sichuan Road, from Wuxian County, Jiangsu, died of illness on July 11 of this year. His position and property were all inherited by his adopted son, Zhongfang (45 years old, residing at No. 29, Jiwu Lane, Ximen Road). Ye Huanyu had taken several concubines during his lifetime, who lived separately. One of them, Wu, was also one of Ye's concubines, residing at No. XX, 852 Nong, Chengdu Road. On February 28, 1932, she committed suicide by secretly consuming raw opium due to some reason. She left behind a daughter named Ruizhen, who is now 17 years old. On February 5 of this year, she participated in the sixth group wedding organized by the Municipal Government and married Wu Junqing (also known as Wending, 22 years old, residing at No. 27, Wenzhou Road), who is from the same hometown. Because Ye Zhongfang denies Wu Ye Ruizhen's identity, Wu Ye Ruizhen hired lawyer Li Zhongwen and filed a lawsuit in the First Special District Court against her brother Ye Zhongfang for embezzlement of inheritance. The gist of the complaint is that the plaintiff is the daughter of Ye Huanyu, and the defendant is Ye Huanyu's nephew, who was adopted as his son. After Huan Tu died, the plaintiff returned home to attend the funeral, but the defendant refused to allow her to wear mourning clothes. The plaintiff then sent a letter of inquiry through a lawyer on September 20 and ordered that the inheritance be handed over for division. The defendant replied through a lawyer, saying that Huan Tu had no daughter like the plaintiff, claiming that the inheritance had been used to pay off debts, clearly showing his intention to embezzle the inheritance. As for the plaintiff's identity, there are official and private documents that can prove it. As for Huan Tu's inheritance, there are residential properties in Suzhou, stocks, savings, etc. Therefore, it is requested that he be punished under Article 335, Paragraph 1 of the Criminal Law, and that he be ordered to hand over the entire inheritance for notarization and division by elders of the clan. Yesterday afternoon, Judge Dai Rongduo held a preliminary hearing in Criminal Division 2. Wu Ye Ruizhen first stated her charges. When questioned, Ye Zhongfang stated that he had never seen the plaintiff, so he did not know who she was. When his lawyer received the letter, he investigated and learned that she was the daughter of his deceased father's concubine, so he could not recognize her. The court then asked if he was willing to share Huan Yu's inheritance with her, and he replied that his father had no inheritance to share. The court asked if it was because he could not recognize the plaintiff's identity that he would not share the inheritance, or was it because there was no inheritance to share? He replied that it was because his father had no inheritance. The plaintiff's lawyer Li then presented a copy of the group marriage certificate to prove that Ye Huanyu was the officiant, and requested that the court examine the autopsy records of the Procuratorate after Ye Wu (the plaintiff's mother) committed suicide, as well as the plaintiff's school records when she was studying at the Mei Baige Road Renhe Elementary School in the second semester of 1932 and the first semester of 1933, which could all prove that the plaintiff was indeed Huan Tu's daughter. He also submitted Ye Huanyu's obituary, in which the name of the plaintiff's husband, Wu Wending, was also listed. It was also stated that Ye Huanyu's property included a residence in Suzhou, No. XX Jiuxiang, worth about 8,000 yuan, 2,000 yuan in shares in the Rui Tai Cloth Shop, 3,000 yuan in savings, 1,000 yuan in shares in the Yongyuan Cloth Shop, 8,000 yuan in shares in the Dafeng Factory, 9,000 yuan in claims from acting as a comprador for the Boshen Foreign Firm, and a diamond ring worth 2,000 yuan and a string of pearls pledged by others to Ye Huanyu, etc. The court then asked if the obituary presented by the plaintiff's lawyer was genuine, to which he replied that it was indeed issued by his family. He also invited Hua Maosheng to court and stated that the case should first confirm the plaintiff's identity through civil proceedings. After reviewing the records, the judge announced that the case would be adjourned for further hearing.

Further News on Wang Enzhao's Death by Poisoning 158

Mr. Wang Enzhao, an accountant at the Central Aviation School and formerly the founder and manager of the Dahua Real Estate Company in Shanghai, was invited by a friend to serve as assistant manager of the Jia Hua Bank in the 23rd year of the Republic [1934]. The bank collapsed in the same year. Mr. Wang's nerves were severely stimulated, leading to abnormalities and insomnia. Last year, he transferred to the aviation school. Due to heavy workload, he recently took leave to come to Shanghai for medical treatment. He resided at the Yang residence, number 559 on Route Lafayette [today's Fuxing Middle Road], a relative's home. Unexpectedly, on the night of the 8th, due to persistent insomnia, he took too many sleeping pills, leading to poisoning. It was not until noon on the 9th that the family members of the Yang residence discovered him. They rushed him to the Red Cross Hospital for emergency treatment, but due to the long delay, it was impossible to save him. He passed away at 4:30 PM. His family members then transported the body to the Shanghai Funeral Parlor on Xujiahui Road for the encoffining ceremony at 2:00 PM on the 11th. Over a hundred relatives and friends of the Wang family, including Zhang Yongni, Zhao Jinqing, Qu Wenliu, Huang Ruisheng, Hu Xirong, Hu Jingchuan, Ding Jiwan, and Zhou Jinghan, all went to express their condolences. Mr. Wang is survived by his wife, Mrs. Ding, and two sons, Zhigang and Zhimin, who are still very young, one seven years old and the other six. It is said that Mr. Wang's family was very harmonious. Yesterday's report that there was discord between Mr. Wang's mother-in-law and daughter-in-law was untrue, and the mistaken name of Wang Guangzhu was also a misunderstanding. Mr. Wang's tragic death was caused by insomnia in the near term and by the collapse of the Jia Hua Bank in the long term. Mr. Wang took responsibility too seriously, leading to a pathological condition of his nerves. Mr. Wang was only 34 years old, at the prime of his life, and his sudden passing has left his relatives and friends in deep sorrow and mourning. His coffin is currently temporarily placed in the Shaoxing Guild Hall, and a memorial service will be held on a chosen date.

Letter to the Editor 163

To the Editor: We are writing in response to a report from the Dagong News Agency published in your newspaper on October 12th. After investigation, we find that it differs greatly from the facts. Our factory has always treated its workers generously. Unexpectedly, in the midst of this tense situation, a small number of weaving department workers, including He Gencai and Xu Xuewen, used false pretenses to coerce workers, extort membership fees, and disrupt the machines. Our factory, in addition to legally dismissing those with serious offenses, still maintained its past policy of leniency and issued a sincere notice on the 2nd of this month, urging workers to return to work. Unexpectedly, they became even more aggravated and, on the 7th, led their accomplices to Hengfeng Road to assault workers who came to the factory. On the 9th, they led a crowd to rush into the weaving machine room in an attempt to force a strike and shut down the motors, causing some well-intentioned workers to retreat. Currently, except for a portion of workers in the weaving department who have been forced to stop work, all other departments in our factory are operating as usual. All the detailed circumstances have been reported by our factory to the Municipal Bureau of Social Affairs. We are afraid that the outside world will not understand and be misled, so we are writing to request a prompt correction to clarify the situation. This is to the Editorial Department of the Shen Bao Newspaper. Respectfully, Hongzhang Textile Dyeing Factory, October 12th.

Weather Report 164

The Xujiahui Observatory's weather forecast at 4:30 PM yesterday stated: The weather in the Shandong area is clear and cool, with fairly strong northeast to northwest winds. The wind in the Yellow River basin and the upper reaches of the Yangtze River is light and variable. The middle and lower reaches of the Yangtze River have gentle northerly to northeasterly winds, with morning fog. The East China Sea and Hao Bay are mostly cloudy with strong northeasterly winds. The climate southwest of the Ogasawara Islands is severe due to a hurricane moving north. At 2:00 PM, the center of the first hurricane was within 120 miles of 24 degrees north latitude and 133 degrees east longitude, moving northeast-north. The center of the second hurricane was within 120 miles of 17 degrees north latitude and 120 degrees east longitude, moving northeast. The wind force of both hurricanes is unknown. Also, the highest temperature in Shanghai in the 24 hours before 3:00 PM yesterday was 83.7 degrees, and the lowest was 55.6 degrees. On the same day last year, the highest was 77.9 degrees, and the lowest was 59.2 degrees.

Education News

Jiangsu Province's Flexible Measures for Student Transfers to Vocational Schools Approved by the Ministry of Education and Ordered to be Implemented by Subordinates 165

The Education Department of Jiangsu Province has stated that the province's measures for transferring students to vocational schools are implemented in accordance with the regulations of the Ministry of Education, following Chapter 10 of the regulations for middle schools and normal schools. However, the regulations stipulate that the subjects studied by transfer students must be the same. The department has recently found this regulation to be difficult and has specially requested the Ministry of Education to approve a flexible approach. Students who have completed one semester of ordinary senior or junior high school and wish to transfer to the first semester of the first year of an equivalent vocational school will be allowed to enter the class. However, vocational school students will still not be allowed to transfer to ordinary middle schools or normal schools to indicate restrictions. The Ministry of Education has issued instructions stating: "Noted the report. Approval is granted as proposed. However, vocational schools that accept transfer students must have a study period of three years, and the academic performance of the admitted transfer students in each major subject from their original school must be passing." After receiving the order, the Education Department has instructed its subordinates to comply.

Ministry of Education Today's Broadcast Program 176

Topic: How to Study Agricultural Disciplines

Lecturer: Zhang Boyu

Time: 4:30 PM to 5:00 PM

Frequency: 660

Receiver: Middle Schools

Overview of Japanese Schools in Shanghai (7) - Special Report from This Newspaper 177

— Investigation by Hu Zuyin

9. Teacher Cultivation

Teachers in Japanese schools are all called staff members because they believe that teachers are also a type of official. The school attaches great importance to the cultivation of teachers. The school has research departments for each subject, with the principal appointing a director and several members to hold regular research meetings. Student achievement assessments are conducted at regular intervals to allow teachers to reflect on the effectiveness of teaching and the appropriateness of materials. On commemorative days, teachers take turns giving lectures to children. When famous people from outside the school come to give lectures, teachers also participate in listening.

There are five types of teacher training meetings. The entire faculty and staff meet once a week, chaired by the principal, to discuss important school matters. Teaching method research meetings are held irregularly to discuss theoretical and practical issues related to teaching. Teachers are also required to participate in summer training courses in Japan on a rotating basis and report back to the other teachers upon their return. Grade meetings are attended by teachers responsible for guidance in each grade to thoroughly discuss teaching materials and issues related to guidance and care. Reading and presentation meetings are held frequently, with teachers reporting on the content of the books they have read.

In addition, teachers also have external visits. The principal designates the schools to be visited or the teachers make suggestions which are approved by the principal. Sometimes, the principal may assign teachers to visit and inspect new facilities in various fields and make a report on the inspection upon returning to the school. Teachers may also go to various companies, factories, or research institutes to learn about teaching methods and collect reference materials. Teachers also regularly engage in sports, such as tennis, baseball, table tennis, and volleyball, to improve their physical health.

Reflections on Participating in the World Games and Traveling in Europe - A Postscript to the Sino-British Match (Continued) 178

— Li Huitang

The inspiration from this overseas compatriot who warmly cares about our football team is indeed very touching, and at the same time, it greatly strengthened our courage and increased our infinite vigor. We knew that compared to our first confrontation, we at least had some advantages. This was because we knew the British team's playing style and strategy well, while the British team knew nothing about our Eastern team.

On July 29th, the British team arrived. Their dormitory was only a stone's throw away from ours. As soon as I had the chance, I talked to their coach. I first inquired about their background. He said that four members of the team were from the Scottish GreenPark team (the only amateur team to join the Scottish professional first division), and nine members were from the famous English amateur teams Casuals and Corinthians. The other players were selected from amateur international teams in Ireland and Wales. He also said that they originally did not want to participate, but decided to send a team at the last minute, so they lacked training beforehand. Many of the team members did not even know each other's names. Understanding each other would probably require a lot of hard work quickly. Knowing this, I realized that this British team was a combination of England, Scotland, Ireland, and Wales, and not just the strength of England alone. Bringing together the best players from various regions, their combat power would naturally be very strong. However, we had undergone long-term training and cooperation, while they did not even know each other. This was also a small advantage for us. In the days before the game, whenever they practiced, I secretly observed their strengths and weaknesses. On average, their footwork was better than ours, their kicks were more powerful, their bodies were larger, and their strength was more abundant. Judging from these points alone, it would not be easy for us to deal with them. After arriving in Berlin, they were also very careful and vigilant, avoiding friendly matches, so their tactics could not be investigated. But no matter what, we still held a glimmer of hope in despair and did not completely lose heart.

The Games opened, and there were still six days until the match. Apart from watching track and field and football, it was truly a torturous time. In the Nanyang area, we were accustomed to playing at least three or more games a week. Although it was hard work, we were used to it. This time, we had been resting without playing for more than twenty days, which was indeed a bit uncomfortable in our hearts, and we couldn't sleep soundly at night, eagerly awaiting the arrival of the match. Our entire team was suffering from "Over Anxiety," and this unhealthy mentality was probably one of the reasons for our failure.

Time flew by, and it was August 6th before we knew it. After very careful and close discussions, we put out the following lineup:

Ye Beihua, Tan Jiangbai, Chen Zhenhe, Sun Jinshun

Bao Jiaping, Huang Meishun, Li Huitang, Li Tiansheng, Xu Yahui, Feng Jingxiang, Cao Guicheng

On that day, in addition to the athletes who were participating in other sports, the rest of our delegation were all present to watch the match. The overseas Chinese in Berlin also came to cheer us on, and formed two cheering squads to cheer for our team. Everyone's enthusiasm and kindness were truly appreciated. When the bell rang five times, the two teams walked side by side to the center of the field and bowed to the audience on both sides (according to the rules of the Games). Our team won the toss and chose to have the advantage of facing away from the sun. The great battle erupted, and our team took the offensive in one go, sometimes attacking from the flanks and sometimes attacking from the center. The opponent was caught off guard for a while. For the first fifteen minutes, almost the entire field belonged to our team. Once, Shun got a cross from Guicheng fifteen yards from the goal. If he had stopped and shot, he would have definitely scored, but he was too anxious at the time, and kicked the ball as soon as it arrived, resulting in inaccuracy, and it went out one foot from the post. We lost this ball, which was probably fate. It should be known that in a situation of equal strength, the gain or loss of a goal often determines the outcome. Afterwards, although the British team launched several counterattacks, they did not pose a serious threat. Soon after, I was hit in the abdomen by the opponent's defender, and my breath was blocked. After treatment, I resumed the game. The first half ended without any score. However, the spectators in the field all thought that our team's performance was good and that we had the upper hand. Not being able to win in the first half was actually a precursor to our failure in the second half. Missing a good opportunity is still regrettable even now. After the break, we returned to the field. Our team fought hard for twenty-five minutes, but still no result. It wasn't until the twenty-eighth minute that their right winger crossed the ball, our defender made a mistake, and their left forward broke through the net near the goal, opening the scoring. At this time, our team's strength gradually became insufficient, and the opponent took advantage of their lead to repeatedly threaten us. Finally, within ten minutes, with similar passes, their center forward scored another goal, and the victory or defeat was thus determined. Although our team still put up a desperate fight, and I and Jingxiang took long shots one after another, they were all unsuccessful. When the bell rang, our team was eliminated with a score of two to zero, unable to aspire to the title again, and had to watch others compete for the trophy.

Although we lost this game, our performance was still acceptable, leaving a very good impression and earning very good reviews from the media. We also had a good performance in terms of sportsmanship. However, in my opinion, we did not show our full strength that day. The games in Nanyang, the game against India, the game in Yangon, and the games in Singapore were more exciting and wonderful in comparison. This was probably because of the long break and the "Over-Anxiety" mentioned above. After the game, Shen Siliang told me that he was not very satisfied with the left side of the forward line, which missed more than one good opportunity. According to the observations of our Director Rong and Manager Huang, they both thought that if Ji Liang had been used as goalkeeper that day, both goals could have been saved. I also agree with these three insightful people, because Jinshun and Beihua were both getting fat and slow. Although Jiaping was more experienced and agile as a goalkeeper, due to his height, he was not as brave as Ji Liang in saving dangerous shots. Both goals that day were very close to the goal. If the goalkeeper had been more assertive, he should have come out to save the ball. Afterwards, many people involved said that if we had used the following lineup, the result might have been different:

Zheng Jiliang, Tan Jiangbai, Chen Zhenhe, Ye Beihua

Huang Jiliang, Xu Yahui, Li Huitang, Li Tiansheng, Liang Rongzhao, Feng Jingxiang

Cao Guicheng

Although this argument is not without merit, hindsight is unreliable. How do we know that if we had used the above lineup to face the enemy, we would not have suffered an even more disastrous defeat? My only regret is that the British team was conquered by the mediocre Polish team in the second week due to goalkeeping errors. This comparison made us seem even smaller. In fact, to be honest, apart from physique, strength, and running speed, which we can't catch up with, our skills are not much inferior to others.

"Only after learning do you realize your deficiencies; only after realizing your deficiencies can you reflect on yourself." I only hope that this defeat will give us a good lesson and give us an opportunity to reflect on ourselves after returning home.

Handshake with World Standard Footballer Alex James

Appendix: Our Team's Results After the Games 179

Statistics show that our team played a total of 37 games abroad, winning 24, losing 8, and drawing 5. We scored 124 goals and conceded 74 goals. In Europe, apart from the World Games, we played a total of 9 games, winning 1, drawing 1, and losing 7, scoring 14 goals and conceding 46 goals.

The Municipal National Sports School Held its Opening Ceremony Yesterday 182

The Municipal National Sports School held its opening ceremony at 10:00 AM yesterday at the school site. Classes officially started in the afternoon. The details are as follows:

More than 200 Guests and Students

The auditorium was set up under the west grandstand of the large sports field. The attendees included Principal Wu Tiecheng, Director of General Affairs Song Dazhang, Director of Academic Affairs Fang Wanbang, Director of the Health Bureau Li Tingan, Director of the Public Works Bureau Shen Yi, Director of the Public Security Bureau Cai Jingjun, Director of the Finance Bureau Xu Fu, Chairman of the Municipal Council Wang Xiaolai, as well as the school's faculty, staff, students, and guests, totaling more than 200 people. After the ceremony, Director of General Affairs Song Dazhang reported on the preparations.

Principal Wu Tiecheng Delivered a Speech

Following this, Principal Wu delivered a speech, stating that the municipal government had been planning to establish a comprehensive sports school since building the sports field two years ago. However, due to financial and political circumstances, it had been delayed. Now, stimulated by participating in the World Games, they deeply felt that no matter how difficult it was, they had to establish a sports school as soon as possible, first to fully utilize this great sports field, cultivate qualified sports instructors, and serve the city, in order to correct the one-sided errors in the sports world; and second, to forge a sound physique as the foundation for the revitalization of the nation, striving to integrate sports and military affairs, and cultivate obedient, hardworking, self-governing, brave, mutually helpful, united, and disciplined people from the strict New Life Movement to guide society, break the arrogance of the "sick man of East Asia," and eliminate the morbid state of complacency, complacency, self-abandonment, cowardice, selfishness, and disorder, in order to fulfill the mission of strengthening the country and preserving the race.

Director of Academic Affairs Fang Wanbang's Speech

Subsequently, Director of Academic Affairs Fang Wanbang gave a speech, stating that students should strive to improve in all aspects, including educational principles, sports fundamentals, life philosophy, science, morality, and hygiene. The school's academic plans included three aspects: (1) enriching the curriculum, (2) strict management, and (3) disciplined life. Finally, guest Wang Xiaolai gave a speech, stating that using the sports field to establish a sports school was making the best use of the land and talent. Although there were already three sports schools in Shanghai, none of them were as large as this school. Land and people are the essential elements of a country. A strong nation requires strong people to defend its territory, and then prosperity can be expected. At 12:00, after the group photo, the principal led the guests to visit the school's various facilities, and classes began in the afternoon.

Changes to the Eligibility for the Shanghai Westerners Football Club Cup This Season - Registration Deadline is the 15th, No Extensions Will Be Granted - Strict Restrictions on Nationality Qualifications for International Cup Teams 184

The Shanghai Westerners Football Club has reformed its league organization this season, so the cup restrictions have also been slightly changed. The club has notified all member teams to pay attention. The registration deadline for the cup is set for the 15th of this month. Member teams that wish to participate must complete the registration procedures and pay the registration fee before the deadline. No extensions will be granted. The details are as follows:

Scott Cup

The Scott Cup is open to all member teams (Groups A, B, and C) in the club's league, but they must have the appropriate qualifications. The registration fee is $10 per team. Previously, all league members in each group could participate without restrictions on qualifications.

Zilin Cup

The Zilin Cup is specifically for league members in Groups B and C and member teams that have not participated in the league. The registration fee is $5 per team. Previously, all groups A, B, C, D, and E could participate, and non-league teams were not allowed to join. This spring, it was revised to allow only Groups B and C to participate, but non-league teams are still not allowed. Players who have participated in the Zilin Cup are not allowed to participate in the Junior Cup.

Junior Cup

The Junior Cup is only for Group C league members, Morning League members, and non-league member teams. The registration fee is $5 per team. Previously, all groups B, C, D, and E and non-league teams could participate. This spring, it was revised to allow only Groups D and E and non-league teams to join.

International Cup

The International Cup is for teams representing various countries. The eligibility of each team's players must be officially recognized by the country they represent. Those living in Shanghai must obtain proof of nationality from the relevant country. In addition to the above, if a player does not have an official representative organization in Shanghai to prove their nationality, they can represent the country of their birth. Once a player has been designated to represent a country, they are not allowed to represent another country. There is no registration fee for this competition.

Snippets 187

— (Zhou Mengmo)

How can you get a fruit without a cause? The fruit is originally the price of the cause. Only by planting a cause of hard work and effort can you reap a fruit of success. Friends: Let's not simply lament and be depressed about the harshness of the environment. Know that depression is the grave of ambition; despondency is the trap of self-degradation. Only if we resolutely and bravely rise up, cut through the thorns, and work hard will we have the chance to step onto the bright and splendid road to success.

A small match seems not worth people's attention; but its use, simply experience it in daily life, and you will realize its great contribution to mankind, deeply containing the meaning of "sacrificing oneself for righteousness." We should use it to constantly remind ourselves and learn a lesson: that is, to make our lives fulfilling and valuable, and only by embracing the spirit of sacrifice can we live a good life.

The waves in the sea are turbulent and surging, making shocking sounds, and the destructive power of the water is invincible. This is the power of waves pushing waves, the power of unity. If we, China, with its vast land and abundant resources, can unite as one and constantly strive for self-improvement, will we still sit in sorrow and suffer the tragedy of being invaded by the great powers and losing territory?

Somersaults 188

— Chen Liang

My childhood life in my hometown was happy. When there was a "caotai" opera, it was like the sky falling down. Early in the morning, the guys would put the pine benches on a small cart and push them to the theater to set up the stands. As soon as the opera started, I and the other children were already running around under the stage. Like a wild horse, my mom couldn't control me, and neither could my dad. I couldn't sit still on the stand for a moment. Sesame candy couldn't fool me, and neither could beef dumplings. However, as long as the stage performed martial arts scenes with painted faces doing somersaults, I would climb onto the stand, open my eyes wide, and watch attentively.

Loving to watch somersaults was probably my natural inclination. The skinny monkey with a painted face who could do more than a dozen somersaults in a row was the one I admired the most. The more he sweated and couldn't breathe, the louder my little hands clapped, following others shouting "Good, good, good." Later, a young actor ran out on the stage, about the same age as me, but his somersaults were not good, not agile, and he almost rolled off the stage. I laughed, laughing at his uselessness, thinking: If I did it, I would definitely do better than him.

Later, I actually tried to do a somersault myself. I remember it was when my third aunt was sewing a quilt in the drying yard. I took off my shoes and walked onto the soft cotton batting, bent over, supported myself with my hands, and put my head on the batting, wanting to flip my feet upwards, but it didn't work. I failed once, twice. Finally, with the help of my little uncle, he held my legs up, and I flipped over, but my head was dizzy, my eyes were blurred, and my arms hurt. I could only admire the young actor again, feeling that his skills were a hundred times better than mine, and I shouldn't have laughed at him—

Since I learned that doing somersaults is hard work, every time I see an actor doing somersaults on stage, I can't bear to clap my hands and shout "Good." Taking pleasure in others' suffering, how can that be justified? However, in today's world, people suffer thousands of hardships and can't even get a little applause, let alone sympathy. People are tormented in life, just like doing somersaults. The worst thing is to fall off the stage after a somersault, earning the audience's boisterous "boos."

Occasionally, while drinking with friends in a hotel, I suddenly saw a child who looked about nine years old doing somersaults in front of the table. He didn't do them very well, but he flipped harder and harder. Then, with a pale face, he stretched out his ink-black palms to beg for pennies from the drinkers. This discovery was like a sudden awakening: at such a young age, he was relying on doing somersaults to try to earn a living. Thinking back to the past, I felt a pang of sadness in my heart.

Autumn and Middle Age 189

— Sleeping Buddha

A person's youth is like the first season of the year – spring, with its splendid scenery and vibrant energy, truly beautiful and lovely. Entering adulthood is like summer; though flowers fall and spring fades, the lush green leaves and sturdy branches display great health. The fiery heat, grand ambition, and sharp, soaring spirit resemble the intimidating nature of the blazing summer sun. As one enters middle age, that expansive embrace and courageous spirit gradually dissipate. This is akin to transitioning from summer to autumn. Unknowingly, as the climate progresses, one gradually moves towards desolation. Even oneself is bewildered as to how today's self differs so greatly from yesterday's. As for what happens after autumn? Let that be vague; no need to imagine it further.

"It's hard to be a middle-aged person," "Middle-aged sorrow." If heaven were conscious, it would surely share the same feelings about this season of autumn. Indeed, in every comparison, middle age and autumn, autumn and middle age, are remarkably similar. The unpredictable wind and rain of autumn are like the constant stimulation of life in middle age. The sounds of insects in the autumn fields, so plaintive and yearning, so like weeping and lamenting, are just like a middle-aged person's feeling of being unable to escape the nagging about firewood and rice from his wife, or to alleviate the hunger and cries of his children. The fallen leaves that fill the steps in autumn, swept away only to be replaced by more, are like the frequent disappointments and unshakeable sorrows of middle age. Isn't this cold autumn visage and desolate autumn mood sufficient to symbolize the expression and heart of a middle-aged person? However, autumn also has joys compared to other seasons, such as the exceptionally bright moon in the mid-sky. This is just like the mind of a middle-aged person, which, like a mirror, sees through all the evils of the world, understands all its changes, and has an increasingly clear understanding of the true meaning of life.

Therefore, although autumn is said to be melancholy and sorrowful, only middle-aged people can truly understand and appreciate it, merging with autumn, stirring up melancholy and sorrow into a pile. Youth and adulthood fundamentally lack autumn; where does sorrow come from? Where does grief originate?

Random Musings on the Double Tenth 190

— Zhang Huang

Ten placed side by side form "廿," commonly read as "nian." In the past, there was a princess whose name was twenty (二十), who was favored and held power. People in the folk called the number twenty "nian" to avoid using the name of the princess. This practice has persisted to this day. Therefore, the Double Tenth Festival, established as National Day, should be eternally remembered in the hearts of the people.

The Double Tenth as twenty (廿) also resembles the grass radical in Chinese characters. Is it that this Double Tenth Festival, with its serious, extremely tragic, and passionate significance, in the past history of our Republic of China, has often been carelessly and superficially celebrated during difficult times, so that the number and the symbol coincide, predestined? What we hope for from now on is that for all that can be done to secure the nation's destiny on a foundation of rock, and to advance the Double Tenth Festival to a magnificent and glorious realm, all of us as a nation should strive in the spirit of pioneering and constantly strengthen ourselves. May we see the national spirit on Double Tenth Day in the future be like strong grass in a fierce wind, far from the sight of grass bending before the wind. Wouldn't that be joyous?

A certain gentleman, fond of novelty, suddenly had a whimsical idea. He collected commemorative stamps issued for the Double Tenth Festival of the tenth year of the Republic, insisting that they be those postmarked at 10:00 AM on that day. He actually obtained a complete set: one-cent, three-cent, six-cent, and ten-cent stamps, each with a clear and recognizable postmark. He then mounted them and kept them hidden. This commemorative stamp, marking the twenty-fifth anniversary of the establishment of Chinese post, coming together by chance, is like a surviving treasure. Now, it happens to be the Double Tenth Festival of the twenty-fifth year of the Republic, another coincidence! The stamp features portraits of Xu Shichang and two others, printed in different colors. This old man is also the only surviving treasure among the former presidents of the Republic! The owner recently expressed his intention to "reluctantly part with his coral." Asking about it at the Liangchen Haoyou Society on Beijing Road, five yuan in legal tender could exchange for it. This is also a fine tale for the Double Tenth Festival. Telling the readers, it is permissible to act quickly.

Double is even, and ten is complete. Using these to name the National Day is a well-wishing and auspicious act! However, this is formed by the heroic spirit and hot blood of the martyrs. Looking to the south, the heroic aura of Huanghuagang soars into the clouds. Startling the north, the ghostly flames of the Heilongjiang turn green. If this golden jar is not mended, how can we face the martyrs in the afterlife?
